17.6.3 Discussion on Possible Concep­
tual Vulnerability
When introducing a concept, it is important to avo­
id conceptual vulnerability. Pugh (1991) states that 
it “usually manifests itself in two ways: Either the 
chosen concept is weak due to lack of thoroughness 
in the conceptual approach, or the chosen concept 
is strong, but due to lack of thoroughness in the con­
ceptual approach the reasons for its strength are not 
known or understood”.
The design team has considered the Link Model (Fi­
gure 154) through the process to avoid a lack of tho­
roughness in the conceptual approach. An important 
task in concept selection is thus choosing appropria­
te criteria. The criteria are based on user needs and 
value and developed with the users. This makes con­
cepts strong as the designer and user are linked. The 
idea with and idea in shows this link between the 
concept and the user. Furthermore, the value state­
ments are also reflected in the concept.  Nonetheless, 
it does not asssure feasability.
The design team is also aware of instances where 
the user does not manage their condition in the op­
timal way due to other needs. This was seen with 
the restaurant visit described in the sequence model 
(Section 3.3.3). Even though the user knows what 
the best way to tackle their blood glucose is, it is 
human to do what is easiest and fits the temporary 
needs. It is therefore expected that there is a limit 
for how long users will do the challenges and tho­
roughly track their habits. This is an aspect which is 
difficult to test and approximate.
To put it in perspective, data on how long existing 
apps are used was considered. It showed that it is not 
unusual for the average app to lose 80 % of the users 
==PAGE:157==
157
Figure 154: Link Model
Figure 155: Graph from Quettra, 2015. Quettra soft­
ware resides on over 125M Android devices worldwide, 
collects install and usage statistics of every application 
present on the device. Five months of data starting was 
collected.
during the first week (Figure 155). Such statistics 
can keep everyone from entering the app market. 
Nonetheless, in this specific case, the targeted users 
are very dependent on their apps and tracking is part 
of their routine when estimating their insulin-ne­
ed. Their diabetes related apps are well-integrated 
in their lives and kept for years. So although it is a 
concern with development of apps, the use of an app 
for tracking in combination with the target group is 
not considered conceptually vulnerable.
Furthermore, to avoid conceptual vulnerability, 
users have been closely involved in the develop­
ment and detailing of the concept. This has aided 
the design team in continuously identifying the ne­
cessary - which in the method of Lean UX has been 
described in the Minimal Viable Product (Section 
17.2.2). The core of the concept is its motivating 
and individual learning structure which provides 
the user with overview of how their blood gluco­
se reacts under various circumstances. Contrary, it 
was identified that the Sharing-function is not the 
core of the concept and should therefore not be part 
of the MVP for the first phase of implementation. 
However, it adds strength to the concept as it fulfills 
the needs of belonging through a network of people 
with T1D and self-actualization by helping others 
with T1D (Section 4.2.5) and should therefore be 
implemented next.
While close user involvement ensures that the user’s 
value perception is linked with the design team’s 
reasoning, it also entails a risk of accepting loose 
ideas as being needs of the user, which could lead 
to conceptual vulnerability. The design team must 
therefore listen openly while safeguarding the core 
of the concept. This was the case when it was sug­
gested to include competitions between users during 
the third iteration. This was assessed to stray too far 
from the focus on individuality though it may be a 
good feature.
==PAGE:158==
The initial project plan for Detailing & Justifi­
cation made in the Gantt chart (Appendix 1) 
differed quite a lot from the activities found re­
levant when the project had progressed to this 
phase. However, this was expected since it was 
difficult to foresee the activities of this phase 
before the task had been scoped and the solu­
tion space had been explored. 
The activities listed in the initial Gantt chart had 
taken their starting point in a typical product 
design project. For instance, it was unknown if 
Lean UX would be used or methods from me­
chanical design, e.g., quantitative- and prin­
ciple structure drawings (Tjalve, E., 2003) and 
material considerations for development of the 
chosen concept. 
18 Reflection on Detailing & Justification
158
As emphasized in contextual design (Holtzblatt, 
K., & Beyer, H., 1997), the reason for building 
paper prototypes is to support the conversa­
tion between user and designer. It must the­
refore be easy to modify the fields to support 
the conversation. As the sessions were done 
online, the conversation was less interactive 
than it would usually be when using paper pro­
totyping. The advantage of the paper proto­
type is that it is easy to modify by everyone, 
regardless of design experience, therefore did 
not serve its full purpose. In a physical sessi­
on, it would be quick for the test participant to 
modify the prototype. For the online sessions, 
it was more effective to do it in spoken words.
==PAGE:159==
Continuous usability testing and a final user va­
lidation showed that the final concept, Exerci­
seExpert, fulfills the need of the users by crea­
ting a better structure for obtaining insights on 
blood glucose levels in relation to exercise. 
The concept was detailed to include statistics 
on blood glucose in relation to exercise and 
the options to put it in relation to food intake 
and mood.
A gold-, silver- and bronze solution was made 
and the design team proposes the gold so­
lution. However, it is recommended that The 
Danish Diabetes Association work further on 
the bronze solution as it would be within their 
19 Summarization of Detailing & 
Justification
competencies and resources and can function 
as proof of concept for the gold solution.
 
The design team evaluated the final concept to 
fulfill the design task and the goal.

==PAGE:161==
In this Master Thesis, the design team repre­
sents The Technical University of Denmark 
(DTU) and has formed a partnership with The 
Danish Diabetes Association. Thus, the design 
team is responsible for ensuring knowledge ex­
change, which is “the give-and-take of people, 
20 Knowledge Exchange
Education 
An important part of knowledge exchan­
ge is the four educational practises which 
have developed the knowledge and skill 
set of the design team to be able to con­
tribute to society. The design team has 
shared deep working knowledge by in­
cluding The Danish Diabetes Association 
in the process and demonstrating how 
they can use design methods and theory 
on real problems.
Research
The discoveries of this thesis are obtained 
under the research practice Centres of re­
search, education and innovation. While 
DTU can be categorized as such a Centre, 
the design team has only partially taken 
part in the integrated community, though 
following the principles of “timely, direct, 
and implementable research, education, 
Figure 156: Illustration from Crawley, E. et al., 2020.
capacities, and ideas between the university 
and its partners” (Crawley, E. et al., 2020). This 
section describes how the design team has 
applied academic practices within the overlap­
ping domains of education, research, and cata­
lyzing innovations (Figure 156). 
161
and innovation outcomes that impact society” 
(Crawley, E. et al, 2020).
The discoveries made are exchanged with The 
Danish Diabetes Association through presen­
tations (Section 20.1) and handovers (Section 
20.2 & 20.3).
Catalyzing Innovations
The design team tries to catalyze innovation 
with the objective to develop a life improving 
concept for people with T1D, thus to create so­
cietal impact. A concept has been synthesized 
but the knowledge needs to be exchanged 
with partners in the industry in order to create 
actual innovation (Crawley, E. et al, 2020). This 
has been done through the facilitation of dia­
logue with various possible partners who were 
identified as having incentive to take part in 
the implementation of the concept.
The Danish Diabetes Association is one of the­
se partners though with limitations to the scale 
of the concept. Therefore a recommendation is 
given in Section 20.4 for how they can create 
innovation by applying the discoveries of the 
project.

20.1 Presentations of Discover­
ies for Stakeholders within the 
Danish Diabetes Association
Various stakeholders within The Danish Diabetes 
Association were included in the process through 
shorter weekly meetings, monthly status meetings 
(presenting the work done the past month), as well 
as presentations for larger groups concluding each 
phase of the project.
At the end of the Exploration phase, the conducted 
research and analysis were presented. The work mo­
dels functioned as a means to exchange knowledge 
about specific instances of discoveries whereas the 
affinity diagram was used to both demonstrate how 
to reveal common issues and themes and to discuss 
these. Though the presented discoveries were not 
unfamiliar to the stakeholders within The Danish 
Diabetes Association, the new perspective was sub­
sequently used for defining problematic areas used 
for giving out research grants. These were shared on 
the website, Facebook and Instagram association’s 
members could vote for an area of interest. A snip­
pet from the website can be seen on Figure 157.
In the presentation at the end of the Concept Synthe­
sis phase, the focus was mainly on the synthesized 
concepts. This resulted in both valuable feedback 
for the design team, used for evaluating the con­
cepts, as well as realizations for The Danish Diabe­
tes Association. The concepts involving their webs­
ite made the involved stakeholders recognize a lack 
in the information material and knowledge provided 
the association.
The final presentation took place after the last pha­
se, Detailing and Justification, was concluded. As 
new stakeholders were involved, this presentation 
encompassed the entire project, thereby ensuring 
that all the reasoning leading to the final concept 
was included. This facilitated the dialogue on how 
The Danish Diabetes Association can take part in 
implementing the concept.
20.2 Handover of Discoveries 
and Concepts for Website 
Implementation
DiabetesConvo and TechGrants Overview Provider 
were not considered to be the action point for the de­
sign team as they did not stand out in either the eva­
luations of the feedback session or the WOM. None­
theless, there has been seen a need that fits into the 
products and competencies within the association.
Everything that led to DiabetesConvo and Tech­
Grants Overview Provider was therefore handed 
over for the association to consider these needs in 
their development of the website.
20.3 Handover of Insights to 
Future Thesis Students
The Danish Diabetes Association has recently star­
ted a collaboration with thesis students to encourage 
more research and development within the field of 
diabetes. The design team had no specific knowled­
ge regarding diabetes before starting this thesis and 
since there was not a predefined area of interven­
tion, it was decided to start broadly. It is therefore 
assumed that future thesis students might encounter 
similar struggles. Thus, the design team proposes to 
communicate the broad research and analysis for 
future students to make sure that the problems they 
try to solve are in line with a holistic view of the per­
sons with T1D. It is also proposed to use the created 
idea catalogue and concept catalogue to inspire 
students with areas of intervention based on their 
expertise and interests. Considerations on further 
work on ExerciseExpert should also be included to 
encourage further development.
The Danish Diabetes Association is currently wor­
king on making a website page for student projects 
which among other things will include a link to this 
thesis (Appendix 17). To catch attention and com­
162
Figure 157: How The Danish Diabetes Association has 
used the problematic areas.
==PAGE:163==
municate the concept and areas for further work, vi­
sual elements should be included. The design team’s 
suggestion for the website page can be seen in Fi­
gure 158.
20.3 Recommendation for the 
Danish Diabetes Association
It is recommended that The Danish Diabetes Asso­
ciation proceed with the bronze solution as it can be 
implemented within the existing competencies and 
resources of the organization. However, the bronze 
solution should not be viewed as an isolated solu­
tion. It should instead be seen as the first step tow­
ards the gold solution, where The Danish Diabetes 
Association can act as a catalyst for innovation. In 
this context it can be considered a low-fidelity pro­
totype for validating the effect, value, and market 
of the solution. To do so, they must measure certain 
metrics before and after use of the solution such as 
their members’:
•	 Knowledge in the area
•	 Amount of exercise in a week
•	 Ability to predict the blood glucose when exer­
cising
Alternatively, the satisfaction with using the soluti­
on could also be measured.

==PAGE:164==
Exploration
In the Exploration, there has been an open ap­
proach to the area of living with type 1 diabe­
tes (T1D). The design team evaluates that the 
open approach with close involvement of a lar­
ge group of persons with T1D has given a trust­
worthy analysis of common themes and issues 
of having T1D. The Exploration showed that 
unpredictability and individuality were some 
of the largest factors for themes and issues re­
lated to living with T1D. The unpredictability 
is enlarged when exercising and in scenarios 
which can cause stress, e.g., an exam period. 
Ideas were generated throughout the project 
and 109 ideas were collected in an idea cata­
logue as well as 17 ideas based on a co-crea­
tion workshop with potential users which were 
collected in an additional idea catalogue. A 
broad basis for concept synthesis has thereby 
been conducted.
Concept Synthesis
The ideas were used to inspire solutions to 
scenarios by combining them and developing 
them into concepts. 9 diverse concepts were 
included in a concept catalogue which was 
21 Conclusion
164
evaluated by 10 potential users and by syste­
matic methods by the design team. The design 
team considers the evaluation to be extensive 
enough to choose an overall concept which 
is both relevant within the work of the design 
team and The Danish Diabetes Association 
and which is conforming to the users’ needs. 
Detailing & Justification
A function-means-tree and morphology has 
been used to avoid only having one way of for­
ming the overall concept in mind. Usability has 
been thoroughly tested and continuous input 
has been given by potential users. The detail­
ing level is considered to be appropriate for 
the conceptual level of the project, as there are 
only narrow UI/UX design considerations left 
(e.g., color choices). 
The final concept, ExerciseExpert, solves the 
persons with T1D’s need for increasing pre­
dictability by giving them a tool to learn and 
self-observe their blood glucose patterns. 
ExerciseExpert is justified by a user validation 
as well as a judgement by the design based 
on the goal formulation and impact on the 
engineering system. It is evaluated that it fits 
the target group of 18-40 year olds based on 
quantitative data and on user validation with 
potential users.
The implementation of concept has been con­
sidered on three levels, a gold-, silver-, and 
bronze solution, and strengths and weaknesses 
of making a light version of the concept has 
been evaluated. The silver solution, integration 
in another app, is not necessarily easier as it 
has to fit the other app’s business strategy and 
prioritization.  The bronze solution, however, is 
easy for The Danish Diabetes Association to in­
troduce. Nonetheless, it has many large weak­
nesses compared to the gold solution such as 
not including options for tracking and remin­
ders. On the other hand, it can function as a 
stepping stone for the gold solution as it has 
the dual function of being a low-fidelity pro­
totype for testing the gold solution in context. 
Further Work
The concept has not been tested in context 
which is needed to tell if the concept has a 
proven effect on learning. The proven effect is 
crucial for funding and development within the 
medical sector. 
==PAGE:165==
22 Reflection on the Process
165
It is in the nature of a design process to be ite­
rative (Cross, N., 2008), thus it can be challen­
ging to prescribe as done in the initial project 
plan supported by Gantt charts (Appendix 1) . 
However, it is an important part of project ma­
nagement to make a plan in order to ensure 
sufficient time allocated for the various activiti­
es. The plan will inherently change as the pro­
ject progresses, which is reflected upon in this 
section.
Furthermore, the Covid-19 situation in Den­
mark has had a significant impact on the pro­
ject and has forced the design team to rethink 
the approach to some tasks. The situation has 
had both positive and negative implications to 
the project, which is also elaborated in this se­
ction.
==PAGE:166==
22.1 Reflection on Project Plan
The Triple Diamond fits relatively well with the ac­
tual process of the Exploration and Concept Synthe­
sis phases while it showed to not be as descriptive 
for Detailing & Justification. The model depicts De­
tail as solely diverging and Justify as solely conver­
ging, however, the activities overlapped and were 
concurrent. Thus these activities should be seen as 
both diverging and converging and done in parallel.
22.2 Structure of the Project
The Gantt charts used to plan and manage the pro­
ject were adjusted as the project progressed. The re­
vised Gantt charts can be seen in Appendix 1. While 
the activities of the Exploration phase fits the initial 
plan relatively well, considerable adjustments were 
needed for the later phases. As the design team had 
chosen to explore a broad problem space, the cor­
responding solution space was also broad. This has 
been a characteristic of the project which made it 
difficult to select relevant methods and theory when 
planning. The broad solution space thereby meant 
that the design team had to rethink the activities of 
the Concept Synthesis phase as it in example did not 
make sense to use function-means-tree or morpho­
logy as systematic ideation methods when creating 
concepts. Similarly, the Detailing & Justification 
phase needed to be adjusted to entail activities rele­
vant for the chosen concept.
Overall the Gantt charts served well as means to 
manage the time during the project. There have only 
been a few instances where activities were delayed, 
the most significant being the final user validation 
which ended up being delayed by one and a half 
weeks. This meant that the Detailing & Justification 
phase had to be extended a few days. However, as 
the design team had anticipated changes to the initi­
al plan, the final two weeks of the project had been 
reserved as buffer time and report writing.
Stakeholder involvement
The stakeholder involvement has mainly consisted 
of involvement of persons with T1D. These were 
mostly within the specified target group (18-40-year-
olds) though older type 1 diabetics were also inclu­
ded to understand whether a possible solution could 
fit into their context as well. Only a few other ty­
pes of actors were involved during Exploration and 
Concept Synthesis. It could have added new insights 
to involve more stakeholders within the treatment 
team especially regarding how a possible solution 
could be implemented. To cover this aspect, vario­
us stakeholders were involved during Detailing & 
Justification. Though it could have been beneficial 
to create an understanding of implementation earlier 
on in the project it is not considered a big weakness 
of the project as the focus has been on creating life 
improvement for type 1 diabetics, why this interac­
tion has been prioritized.
22.3 Reflection on Implications 
of Covid-19
The project was conducted under the circumstances 
of Covid-19, where the Danish society has been in 
various degrees of lock-down. Therefore the majo­
rity of stakeholder involvement was done online. 
This form of involvement ensured that the design 
team could involve a large number of users from all 
parts of Denmark as well as one living in Sweden. 
Furthermore, this revealed how the geographical lo­
cation of the user impacts their treatment opportuni­
ties, which has been an important factor to include 
when developing concepts and which partially in­
spired one of the developed concepts.
However, the online meetings have also had nega­
tive implications such as limiting the opportunities 
of conducting contextual inquiries and approaches 
for interaction. Especially design games, which can 
function as useful boundary objects, were difficult 
to do online. The participants tended to only talk and 
seemed apprehensive to use the created design ga­
mes, e.g. a slideshow with blank boxes for creating 
a sequence of actions.
Additionally, the digital format could in some cases 
present challenges for some of the participants who 
were not as used to conducting online meetings. I.e. 
one of the usability tests had to be done indirectly 
where the design team had to present the prototype, 
as the participant had troubles with opening it and 
sharing the screen.
The Covid-19 situation can also have been a factor 
which impacted the number of participants in the 
co-creation workshop, as it was conducted during a 
time where many people were still cautious. How­
ever, it is recognized that it in general can be inti­
midating to sign up for a workshop, why Covid-19 
cannot be said to be the sole reason for only having 
two participants. In contrast, the Covid-19 situation 
was directly stated to be the reason why the majori­
ty of the doctors and nurses contacted did not have 
time for interviews during the Exploration phase.
166
==PAGE:167==
Lastly, though the concept ExerciseExpert was not 
chosen because of its digital format, it was a benefit 
for detailing and testing. As an app concept it was 
possible to make digital prototypes, thus testing and 
iterating could be done satisfactorily online. If it had 
been a physical product, the user involvement in the 
last phase would have required more work-arounds 
and planning in order to conduct it online.
167

Appendix 3: 
Interview Guide (Potential 
Users)
Intro
Present us:
•	
Julie and Catharina
•	
Studies Design and Innovation at DTU - this is our master thesis. 
Present the project:
•	
Purpose: To develop a concept for life improvement of people with type 1 diabetes. 
•	
Status: We are in the first phase of the project, where we have an open approach to explore the field and issues there might be. 
•	
Your input: Will give us an insight to an everyday life with diabetes - e.g. what takes a lot of energy, good and bad.
•	
What can it result in? No law changes, etc. Physical product, apps, information enhancement.
•	
It must be maintained by the Danish Diabetes Association so that it cannot be a redesign of other people’s (e.g. Novo Nordisk’s) products. 
But it can be accessories that help the use of it.
Formali­
ties
May we record the interview and / or take pictures along the way? We can easily blur your face in pictures if you do not want to appear in our 
report, for example.
Open 
questions
•	
What type of diabetes do you have and when were you diagnosed?
•	
What kinds of medicine are you taking in relation to your diabetes?
•	
Which products do you use in connection to your diabetes?
•	
To take your medicine or make everyday life with diabetes easier? (E.g. pens, insulin pump, glucometer, sensor, apps or notebooks, 
etc.)
•	
How do you get/ did you get these products? What was the process? (through municipality, hospital, etc.?) How do/did you experience 
this process?
Answer:
•	
When was the last time you experienced challenges related to your diabetes?
•	
In what contexts do you often experience challenges?
•	
What contexts are easier to be in?
•	
Are there any contexts where you feel hindered by your diabetes and can not do the same as others? Which ones? Why? 
Answer:
Questions added along the way are marked in bold.
Questions which we stopped asking along the way 
are marked in grey.
XII
==PAGE:184==
Storage
•	
How do you store your different types of medicine and diabetes products?
•	
Where and how is it stored at home?
•	
What do you always have on you?
•	
Where and how is it stored when you are out? Is it different depending on the situation (school/work, restaurant visit, party, etc.)?
•	
Have you experienced challenges with storing your medicine and other products (e.g. with keeping it 2-8 °C)? When and in which con­
text? (e.g. last time you experienced it)
•	
Have you experienced challenges with keeping track of your stock of medicine and other products?
•	
Have you experienced challenges with not packing enough medicine or other products? (e.g. for a normal day, for a trip, etc.)
Answer:
Products
•	
How often do you have _____ on you?
•	
Have you experienced situations where you were missing ____?
•	
What works well about ___?
•	
What does not work well about ____?
•	
Have you been recommended to use other products?
•	
Have you experienced that any products have broken?
Answer:
Extra - 
specifical­
ly about 
pumps 
and 
sensors
•	
When did you get your pump and/or sensor?
•	
How was the process around getting the pump and/or sensor?
Answer:
Measure­
ment of 
blood 
glucose
•	
How often do you measure your blood sugar? Why?
•	
Do you track your measurements? How?
•	
How often do you experience it being too high or too low? Can you tell us about when and why it happened last time?
Answer:
XIII
==PAGE:185==
Diet and 
exercise
•	
Have you developed any dietary routines due to your diabetes?
•	
How do you count carbs?
•	
Did you use to count carbs differently?
•	
Have experienced a need to count more precisely?
•	
What is the biggest hindering of you counting?
•	
Is there any food/drinks you always have with you?
•	
Have you developed any routines for exercise due to your diabetes?
Answer:
Consulta­
tions
•	
How is the consultations with your doctor/nurse usually structured?
•	
What do you get out of your consultations?
•	
What are you missing from your consultations?
Answer:
Final 
comments
Is there anything else you think might be relevant to talk about? 
Answer:
Round-off
Thank you so much for your time and your openness - it adds huge value to our project.
Further 
contact
May we contact you again later in our process, for example to participate in workshops for concept development or feedback of concepts?

Appendix 4: Interview Guide 
(Treatment Team)
XVI
Intro
Present us:
Julie and Catharina
Studies Design and Innovation at DTU - this is our master thesis. 
Present the project:
Purpose: To develop a concept for life improvement of people with type 1 diabetes. 
Status: We are in the first phase of the project, where we have explored the field and gained insights into the everyday life of persons with 
T1D and uncovered the experienced issues
Your input: We want to uncover the relation between the treatment team (doctors, nurses) and the patient. We want to obtain insights into the 
role of the treatment person
Formalities
May we record the interview and / or take pictures along the way? We can easily blur your face in pictures if you do not want to appear in our 
report, for example.
The role of 
the treat­
ment team
What is your role in the treatment process of a T1D patient?
How often are you in contact with a particular patient?
What tasks do you have in the treatment process?
What do you see as your most important task in this role?
Start of tre­
atment
How is a treatment process formed?
What parameters are used?
What is important to explain to the patient when a treatment progress begins?
Which remedies are used in relation to the treatment? (e.g. apps, notebooks, posters, etc.)
Adjustment 
of treatment
How and why is the treatment adjusted? 
Which challenges do you face as a doctor when following the treatment and making adjustments?
Time for 
extra com­
ments
Is there anything else which you think could be relevant to talk about?
Closing re­
mark
Thank you so much for your time - It adds a lot of value for our project.
==PAGE:187==
Appendix 5: 
Interview with Chief Physician 
Henrik Ullits Andersen (Chief 
Physician of the Type 1 Cli­
nic at Steno Diabetes Center 
Copenhagen)
Intro
Present us:
Julie and Catharina
Studies Design and Innovation at DTU - this is our master thesis. 
Present the project:
Purpose: To develop a concept for life improvement of people with type 1 diabetes. 
Status: We are in the first phase of the project, where we have explored the field and gained insights into the everyday life of persons with 
T1D and uncovered the experienced issues
Your input: We want to uncover the relation between the treatment team (doctors, nurses) and the patient. We want to obtain insights into the 
role of the treatment person
Formalities
May we record the interview and / or take pictures along the way? We can easily blur your face in pictures if you do not want to appear in our 
report, for example.
The role of 
the 
treatment 
team
What is your role in the treatment process of a T1D patient?
How often are you in contact with a particular patient?
What tasks do you have in the treatment process?
What do you see as your most important task in this role?
Answers:
•	
selv behandler
•	
team leder sammen med afdelings sygeplejerske
•	
enkelt: 1-4 gange om året afhængig af behov, samtale 20-40 min.
•	
blodprøver ind i mellem. Kontakt hvis der er brug for ændring i behandling.
•	
Ind imellem møder: .. type1 livslang. Første år 10-12 gange og så sjældnere og sjældnere.
•	
Hotline 24/7 eller skrive i min Sundhedsplatform. F.eks. mangler recept eller ønsker hjælpemidler fra kommunen og derfor har brug for 
lægeerklæring. Forskelligt hvor meget der kan klares på tlf. Hvis patienten har det meget dårligt, så får de en hurtigere tid.
•	
Vigtigst: Aflæst blodsukker kurver og komme med forslag til justeringer eller ændre til f.eks. sensor eller anden insulin.
XVII
==PAGE:188==
Start of
treatment
How is a treatment process formed?
What parameters are used?
What is important to explain to the patient when a treatment progress begins?
Which remedies are used in relation to the treatment? (e.g. apps, notebooks, posters, etc.)

Answers:
•	
Ny diag: 10-12 pr år.
•	
Flyttet: Vurdere på første møde.
•	
Andre parametre: Typisk blodsukker relateret.. Derudover: Screene for senfølger. Blodtryk (evt. ekstra konsultation). 
•	
Alm øjne: Hver 2. år (jo værre, jo oftere - ned til 3 mån). Behandling i Glostrups øjenafdeling.
•	
Forklaring ny diag: Krops fysiologi. Hvad gør kroppen i forhold til insulin. Hvilke risici er der. Alkohol. Kvinder: Graviditet. Arbejdsrela­
teret. Mest mundtligt. Måske er der nogle pjecer, ja.. men det er lidt outdated. Det er bedre at det er digitalt - arbejdes der på.
•	
Nogen er lettet over at det er diabetes (frygter kræft). Nogen kender til frygtscenarier fra bekendte (øjne). Det at have en kronisk sygdom i 
det hele taget. Alt har konsekvenser, motion og afslapning. Understøtte personen, at andre kan klatre bjerge osv, og at der ikke behøves at 
skære ned pga. diabetes. 
•	
Freestyle (Libre View) - godt, kan kigge med ved samtale, også godt i coronatider. diasend, CareLink. Efter upload: Henrik kigger dagen 
efter og skriver tilbage. 
•	
Sygeplejerske kan vise muligheder for devices.
XVIII
==PAGE:189==
Adjustment 
of treatment
How and why is the treatment adjusted? 
Which challenges do you face as a doctor when following the treatment and making adjustments?
Answers:
•	
Typisk kigger på 14-30 dages blodsukker. Stikprøve. Spørger om det er repræsentativt? (ferie eller andet: Tilbage i tiden) 
•	
Blodsukkerapparat kan også uploades. Nogen, men færre og færre, skriver blodsukker ned i en bog.
•	
6: Gennemskue problemet - men det kan være svært. Derfor også svært at finde en løsning. Eller at man har den gyldne løsning, men 
patienten ikke er med på det.
•	
Drejer på skærmen og ser med på data. 
•	
Sagtens være at man skal hjem og tænke på noget. Nogle kan selvfølgelig glemme
Give information om sensor, pumpe, injektions
- først og fremmest behandlere
Instruks: Plan for at afprøve forskellige ting. Starter simpelt og billigt. 
Pligt at være opdateret. Nogle gange bringer det op: God idé eller ikke den rigtige løsning for den person.
Libre: Vanskelige regler, Kommunalt: Hvis det er hjælpemiddel, Regionalt: Behandlingsredskab, pumpe & sensor m. alarm. ← mere op til 
dem.
Tilsendt skema, eller nogle tilfælde snakke med sagsbehandler om ting der ikke er helt klare.
Time for 
extra 
comments
Is there anything else which you think could be relevant to talk about?
Closing 
remark
Thank you so much for your time - It adds a lot of value for our project.

Appendix 6: 
Idea Catalogue
Most of the icons used in the Idea Catalogue are not 
made by the design team. They are from open-sour­
ce clip art websites (flaticon.com, icons-for-free.
com and freepik.com). The sensor sticker drawing 
is based on https://www.mysugarcase.com/us/zig­
zag-sensor-sticker-freestyle-libre.html 
XX
Ease of implementation (impl.) and level of in­
novation (inno.) of each idea is assessed on a 
scale from 1 to 10, where 10 is given for the 
ones considered most easy to implement or 
most innovative. E.g.:
impl.: 3/10     inno.: 6/10
Each idea is also color coded by domain to 
communicate who could work with the idea. A 
color legend is present on all pages.
Set for making holes in clothing
Help to do it without getting
an ugly result (for pump tube).
Injection port
With room for a dose and
release when eating. Can
also allow for wearing
bodystockings etc.
Bands/velcro/attachment for placing the 
pump
Allows the user to wear
what they want.
Sensor stickers
To cover sensor with 
decorative print as well as
for providing waterproof
functionality and ensuring 
that the sensor stays on.
The technology is too clumsy
Community          Object for e.g. industrial designer          Programming          Marketing          Health professional      Work process engineer
Tube
Devices as accessories
Instead of covering the
devices, e.g. sensors,

XXVI
Appendix 7: 
Workshop Plan
Workshop
Facilitator: Catharina
Documenter: Julie
Duration: 2 hours
Theme of workshop (Goal statement):
Increase predictability for young adults who have been diagnosed with T1D for more than 2 years.
Purpose
Include potential users in the design process to gain their perspective on the problematic situations and to have them generate and develop ideas on
how to improve the situation
Expected outcome of workshop:
Deeper knowledge of the chosen area, Generated ideas and vague concepts
Snacks (Covid-19 portion-served)
Materials (Atmosphere)
Materials (Exercises)
-
Water (e.g. with fresh oranges or lime)
-
Unsalted nuts (low glycemic snack)
-
Berries  (low glycemic snack)
-
Whole grain crackers  (low glycemic
snack)
-
Chocolate (or similar)
-
Juice or Mentos in case of low blood
glucose
-
(cups for drinks and for dividing snacks)
-
Posters/signs to guide and welcome
-
Speaker (for background music)
-
Printed agenda and rules
-
Wayfinding
-
Pictures or items which can kickstart
ideas
-
T1D memes
-
Scenarios
-
Simple drawings (to illustrate that
it does not have to look nice to
make its point)

cardboard
-

==PAGE:207==
XXVII
Create comfort (~20 minutes)
-
good idea to do exercises which somehow relates to the topic or where the outcome can be used for later
Introduce everyone (5 min):
Plenum, sitting/standing
-
everyone writes their name on a post-it note as well as a number between 1-5, and stick it on their chest
-
takes turns to present their name and x number of fun facts matching the number they wrote
5 ﬂaws (5 min):
In pairs, standing
-
In pairs look at each other for 20 seconds
-
Turn your back to each other and change 5 things about your apparel
-
turn around again and find the five changes
Squiggle birds (5 min):
Individual (show result to each other), sitting
-
Ask the participants to draw a squiggle
-
Ask them to convert that squiggle into a [Bird, face, plant]
-
The point is to make them believe that every idea is valid and even if it looks useless can actually be transformed into something valuable
==PAGE:208==
-
Hvornår måtte du sidst udskyde eller ændre dine planer pga. type 1 diabetes? Fx aflyse en aftale, vente med at køre bil, blive længere
oppe inden du gik i seng, etc.
-
present and discuss together (additional post-its can be added)
User journey (10 min):
In pairs/all, standing at board, walking back and forth
-
(A day with diabetes decisions)
-
post-its from brainstorming is placed on the journey
-
More is added together :
●
Hvornår i løbet af dagen tager I beslutninger pga. type 1 diabetes?
●
Hvad kan der ske, som gør det ekstra vanskeligt?
-
After 5 minutes the scenarios can be given for further inspiration
5 whys (10 min):
Individual, sitting
-
Put one problem/issue (post-it note) on a piece of paper (from user journey)
-
ask yourself why does this problem occur and add next post-it note with a reason
-
… until ‘why’ has been asked 5 times
Stage discussion (~30 minutes)
-
dive into the focus area
-
create foundation for idea generation
Type 1 diabetes in everyday life (10 min)
(Situations when diabetes is unpredictable)
Individual, sitting
-
3 x 2 min individual brainstorming
-
Hvornår oplevede du sidst, at håndteringen af type 1 diabetes fyldte meget i din hverdag?
-
Hvornår oplevede du sidst, at din krop reagerede på en uventet måde? Fx i forbindelse med motion, eksaminer, varmt eller koldt vejr,
etc.
XXVIII
==PAGE:209==
XXIX
Grouping ideas (15 min)
All together/pairs, standing
-
Group ideas together if they are:
-
same or similar
-
fit in combination with each other
Further development (12 min)
Individual, standing/walking
-
make ideas into something tangible - Build solutions, make tangible - e.g. have stuff lying around that the participants can use to communicate
their ideas
-
Everyone starts at their own group
-
Add one new elements to idea groupings: an idea, wishes for funktions, name, drawing, explanation of what it is or can do
-
After adding one element, they proceed to another available grouping
Develop together (~40 minutes or 50 min)
Individual brainstorming/brainwriting (10 min)
Individual, sitting
-
3x2 min (specific instructions for each round)
-
e.g. Add solutions for user journey or 5 whys - write, draw, build
-
present ideas to each other and add to wall
Group brainstorming (10 min)
All together, standing
-
adding additional ideas together
-
starting point ‘5 whys’, user journey, or each other’s ideas - write, draw, build

Appendix 9: Feedback 
sessions
Plan and questions:
•	 Present the concepts
•	 Name, drawings, description
•	 Idea with, idea in (not on slide)
•	 The difference that matters
•	 Feedback for each concept
•	 First reactions
•	 What do you like about this concept? 
Why?
•	 What do you not like about this concept? 
Why?
•	 Do you see yourself using this concept? 
Why/Why not?
•	 Prioritization of concepts
•	 List the concepts from the one you like 
the best/see yourself most likely to use 
to the one you like the least/see as most 
unlikely to use

Appendix 10: The Danish Dia­
betes Association’s plan for 
work on the website
Note by Karsten Dyrebjerg:
Hvad går vi videre med?
Guides på hjemmesiden.
Nedenstående guides vil blive placeret under råd­
givningen. Det er der de oplysninger giver mening 
i forhold til emnerne.
- Guide til flytning fra en kommune til en anden.
- Guide til hvordan klager man over hjælpemidler.
	
- Klage over afgørelse
	
- Klage over kvalitet
- Guide til rettigheder
	
- Under 18 år
	
- overgang fra barn til voksen
	
- overgang fra voksen til pensionist
Teknologi 
	
- teknologi ligger allerede under diabetes
	
1. https://diabetes.dk/diabetes-1/fak
	
ta-om-type-1/blodsukker-og-maling
	
Det er umiddelbart der vi tænker det hører
	
til jf. ny hjemmeside og de brugerrejser der 	
	
er udarbejdet i forbindelse med opbygning 	
	
af ny hjemmeside.

Hvis man er fysisk aktiv i 
længere tid end 30 
minutter, kan det være 
nødvendigt at spise nogle 
hurtige kulhydrater hver 30-
45 minut under træningen 
og lige efter
Stresshorm
oner såsom 
adrenalin 
og kortisol 
kan få 
blodsukker
et til at 
stige
Musklernes 
øgede 
følsomhed 
over for insulin 
kan vare 1-2 
døgn efter 
træningen
Aerob 
træning kan 
fx være 
gang, 
cykling, 
jogging og 
svømning
mellem 7 mmol/L og 15 
mmol/L før man skal 
motionere anaerobt eller 
af høj intensitet, kan 
træningen som 
udgangspunkt 
påbegyndes men man bør 
være opmærksom at

Anaerob træning eller 
motion af høj intensitet 
kan få blodsukkeret til at 
stige i op til flere timer efter 
motionen er afsluttet
Anaerob træning kan fx 
være vægtløftning, sprint, 
kort distance svømning og 
HIIT træning
Aerob træning er 
gentagne og 
sammenhængende 
bevægelser i længere tid 
typisk af lav til moderat 
intensitet

Appendix 12: 
Main findings from the first ite­
ration, Paper Prototyping
Roland
Main findings - summary
1.	 Prefers a level structure because one needs to 
earn the right to unlock a level and learn from 
mistakes rather than move on too quickly.
2.	 Does not necessarily want to skip any levels as it 
might be good to start from scratch. If he was to 
skip levels, he wants a combination of self-eva­
luation and test.
3.	 Prefers to have less text and more illustrations 
as it supports the text and catches the eye. How­
ever, it is important what the pictures are, as the 
ones shown here might all be aerob but are still 
very different in how a diabetic has to approach 
them. Furthermore, it would be good with the 
option to click the picture and get specific know­
ledge about the exercise type.
4.	 Prefers predefined answers when taking the the­
oretical quiz, as it is too excessive to have to 
write an answer. 
5.	 Prefers to track exercise manually as it becomes 
more fun - though he stated that tracking data is 
really smart, and sees it as the best way to use 
technology. Does not make sense to track pulse 
for him.
6.	 Prefers to manually track other influences - con­
necting with calendar could be an addition.
7.	 Other: To get people started with exercising, the 
first level should be very simple and almost just a 
smiley and blood glucose measurement and then 
the user should be urged to get out and exerci­
se. Then they should just provide a smiley when 
they get back. Furthermore, one should get bad­
ges as a reward when exercising or leveling up, 
however, it is important not to give badges for a 
good blood glucose level.
Signe
Main findings - summary
1.	 Prefers a level structure as one has to work their 
way up, which is both positive and satisfying. 
Furthermore, ‘levels’ sounds better.
2.	 Does not want to skip any levels. Prefers 
self-evaluation as she finds it harsh to get a test 
from the beginning and because one might get 
too far by coincidence. However, states that she 
would probably answer wrongly or give herself 
a bad evaluation to start from the bottom if a 
type of assessment is included.
3.	 Prefers illustrations as they quickly provide in­
formation without having to read carefully and 
give examples which one can relate to.
4.	 Prefers predefined answers especially when il­
lustrations are also used to not have to read an­
swers carefully. A free text answer made her ner­
vous about answering. 
5.	 Does not necessarily prefer to track exercise ma­
nually but does not use anything else to track at 
the moment. It would be nice if the app did it, 
though it does not make sense to track the pulse 
for her.
6.	 Prefers to manually track other influences as she 
wants to feel how her body and mind feels by 
herself - though she also finds it relevant to com­
bine with some automatic tracking for further 
analysis. She is not sure it would make sense to 
track mood but rather symptoms and would also 
prefer to take some notes herself.
Thomas
Main findings - summary
1.	 Prefers a level structure as it guides how he has 
to go through the app and because it is motiva
Hypotheses
H1
The user finds it more motivating to 
learn when the knowledge is divided 
into levels, which needs to be pas­
sed to move on to the next.
H2
The user wants to find out whether 
they can skip some levels when they 
start using the app by taking a test.
H3
The user finds it more motivating to 
learn when less text is used and is 
supported by images.
H4
The user prefers to have predefined 
answers to choose from when taking 
a theoretical quiz.
H5
The user prefers to provide exerci­
se tracking information themselves 
rather than having it tracked automa­
tically.
H6
The user finds it more relevant to 
manually provide information on 
other influences rather than have it 
automated through data from other 
apps.

1.	 ting to see which are completed and which are 
still locked.
2.	 Prefers to have a placement test to find out 
whether he can skip levels. By taking a test he 
also feels assured that he is not missing learning.
3.	 Prefers to have illustrations and short text which 
can quickly be skimmed. The pictures should

Main findings - summary
1.	 Prefers the level structure as it ensures that the 
learning becomes chronological.
2.	 Prefers to self-evaluate rather than take a test 
though this would be difficult because some

other days not

Michael
Main findings - summary
1.	 Prefers the level structure as he does not think 
one should be allowed to go further than they 
are. However, he likes ‘lessons’ for the content 
and then levels could indicate how far you are 
in a lesson.
2.	 Prefers a test to find out where to start and he 
states that it also could be nice if the app asses­
sed his level through some of his fitness data. 
If people had to self-evaluate, there would be a 
risk of people assessing themselves better than 
they are or worse if they are very self critical. 
He would personally be fine with skipping some 
levels but believes that in accordance with gami­
fication it could be good to get through all levels.
3.	 Illustrations would help him but not the ones 
there are now, they would need to communicate 
more precisely - a picture of one running does 
not say whether it is slow or sprint, here text 
would be better. He would prefer a short text but 
there should always be to learn more no matter 
what.
4.	 Prefers predefined answers in either a multiple 
choice quiz or an interactive one. He finds the 
interactive one most fun but stated that it needs 
more precise animations and some text to com­
municate correctly. However, he does not mind 
writing a free text answer but would be doubtful 
about whether the app can assess his answer.
5.	 Wants to track exercise automatically, however, 
the connection should be established first time 
using the app so it does not become a barri­
er before exercising. He does not want to type 
anything manually and if asked to he would defi­
nitely not use the app more once he has finished 
the levels. However, he notes that it might be 
useful for people who do not have other apps 
tracking already.
6.	 Wants other influences to be tracked automa­
tically through a connection with the calendar, 
though it is important that it does not conclude 
anything about his blood glucose but only provi­
des information about differences. Furthermore, 
it has to be able to differentiate between work, 
privat, and exercise calendar. Though he wants 
as much as possible to be automated, he appreci­
ates the mood indications as he sees it as an im­
portant part of getting people to exercise is that 
they get happy from it and generally thinks men­
tal health is neglected in the health care system.
Other: He stated that it might be a good idea to ob­
serve the blood glucose for e.g. two or three hours 
after the workout or maybe get a notification after 
this time span to check blood glucose. He also found 
it important to have 2-3 examples of specific theory 
when learning.

Appendix 13: 
Main findings from the se­
cond iteration, A/B test using 
high-fidelity prototype
Hypotheses
H1
The user prefers to have the option 
to skip the introduction quiz and 
start from level 1.
H2
The user finds it more efficient to get 
the next question as soon as they 
have answered one, without extra 
clicks when taking the introduction 
quiz.
H3
The user can more easily understand 
the knowledge given when learning 
if the illustrations are real photos.
H4
The user finds it more intuitive to 
take the test when there is only one 
space to put answers.
H5
The user prefers to have the option 
to postpone a challenge for later and 
unlock the next theory instead.
H6
The user finds it more motivating 
to register their mood rather than 
symptoms before and after exercise.
Michael
Main findings - summary
1.	 It makes sense to have the option to skip the in­
troduction quiz and start from level 1.
2.	 Finds it efficient to go to the next question 
without pressing submit, as it saves him a click, 
though he finds it important to inform the user 
that they will go to the next question as soon as 
they have clicked. It is also important to inform 
the user whether they answered correctly.
3.	 Prefers real photos, however, it is important that 
different types of sports are represented the same 
in terms of fitness level. It should not be a super 
fit person sprinting and someone with a low fit­
ness level representing jogging - it is easier not 
to offend anyone with animations.
4.	 Prefers to only have one space for answers, as it 
looks better to him. Some may prefer to just tap 
the picture instead of dragging the pictures.
5.	 It is fine to be able to postpone a challenge in 
case the user is in a situation where they cannot 
do the challenge, and fine that it unlocks the next 
theory but it should not unlock anything more. It 
would be good if it then could give a reminder 
to do the challenge - maybe by connecting to the 
calendar, it could be scheduled when to do it.
6.	 Finds mood more motivating than symptoms to 
not urge people to think about symptoms that 
might not be there.
Other: Using the calendar function right after a 
challenge is not directly applicable and it would be 
better as part of a weekly report. After the challen­
ge it would be better with a summary of how the 
blood glucose was before and how it is now as well 
as mood before and after. There should be space for 
one’s own note after an exercise and on a weekly 
report. Badges should be more exciting.
Thomas
Main findings - summary
1.	 Does not want the option to skip the introduc­
tion quiz, as one should just take the quiz and 
not have to think about it. The user will get the 
knowledge from the skipped levels through quiz 
anyways.
2.	 Prefers that it goes to the next question automa­
tically.
3.	 No preferences regarding real photos or animati­
ons, though it might be easier to get a consistent 
look with animations as it quickly can look mes­
sy with real photos portraying many different 
activities.
4.	 Prefers one space for answers when being quiz­
zed. However, it is weird that the pictures be­
come smaller when dragging them to the box. 
Thought it would be possible to just double tap 
to get the image to jump to the box.
5.	 It makes sense to be able to postpone a challen­
ge, though it makes a hole in my levels to unlock 
the next. However, if it was not there he stated 
that he would probably just cheat to move on 
or close the app. The postpone button was too 
small and overlooked.
6.	 Does not find mood more motivating and prefers 
symptoms though they are very connected. He 
is not sure it makes sense to state after the exer­
cise because if he was tired before, he probably 
still is after. However, he stated that symptoms 
can also make one think about it too much and 
‘over-feel’. It would be overwhelming to have 
both. He was also unsure what the mood/symp­
toms input would be used for - if it was for him

Roland
Main findings - summary
1.	 There should not be an introduction quiz to 
skip levels everyone should start from level 1, 
otherwise people do not know what they are 
missing.

pressing submit, as one needs a break to think

make it super easy to understand the informati­

rect answers. It could also be done with clicking

to a level where they can start sharing with

be directly seen in blood glucose and if some­

ver, there are too many moods to choose from, 
it should be a maximum of five. If a user has 
symptoms it is important to stop the user so that 
it does not get dangerous.
Other: Needs some more color (maybe a light back­
ground), some more icons to make it quicker to read 
sports types in the beginning, and more exciting 
badges with fireworks etc. It should be possible to 
add things that one did during the exercise, e.g. if 
something was eaten. The calendar does not have 
much to do with the specific exercise. It would be 
nice if it was possible to see the route of a run if a 
specific route made one more happy. Could be good 
with a checklist and get help to why the blood glu­
cose got low.

Appendix 14: 
Third iteration, think-aloud test
How?
Participants are asked to use the app, while thinking 
aloud. Participants are moderated by questions from 
the design team.
Small tasks were given to ensure that they came 
across screens which would not not be part of a nor­
mal flow:
•	
How would you read about the experiences of 
others? (Sharing)
•	
How would you get an overview of your data? 
(My Profile)
•	
How would you view results or repeat a previ­
ous challenge? (My Challenges)
•	
How would you add a new preferred sport? (Set­
tings)
Likert scale (1-5, where 5 is excellent and 1 is very 
poor):
•	
General experience of the app
•	
General aesthetics of the app
•	
Tone of voice in the app (e.g. whether it is too 
childish, academic, stigmatizing, etc.)
Michael 
Main inputs
Challenge:
•	
It is confusing when to press the finish button 
for a challenge and the red color is not nice to 
indicate it.
•	
It would be nice to also add blood glucose level 
after 12 hours as it can be affected up to 24 hours 
after exercising. This would also help to see the 
bigger perspective as one can feel negatively af­
fected by the exercise in the first couple of hours 
after.
•	
A personal record could be celebrated a little 
more than the other badges - it could be a trophy.
•	
Sharing:
•	
It should always be possible to share, as 
one might need to ask questions and get 
help if they are struggling with something.
•	
It should be possible to report a post if it 
says something factually wrong.
•	
There should be a short introduction when 
entering sharing to say what is allowed to 
share, e.g. people should not give advice 
about treatment. It should also say that it 
is one’s own responsibility.
•	
It would be nice if health professionals 
were also in the app to answer questions 
and give advice.
•	
It should be possible to add more infor­
mation about a profile: how long has one 
had T1D, are they a relative or the patient, 
HbA1c, time in target area, share patterns.
•	
My Profile: It does not make sense to show mi­
nutes spent on theory, it could be the number of 
lessons instead. The user should be able to choo­
se what statistics they want displayed.
•	
Challenges: It would be great to have extra com­
petitions, e.g. “Run a half marathon in 2021” or 
“Compete with others for the most steps”. May­
be an add-on could be to buy a personal trainer 
or someone to give advice.
•	
General experience of the app: 4 
•	
General aesthetics of the app: 4
•	
Tone of voice in the app:5

and type manually.

diabetes symptoms as being sick.

One could be in doubt when to press the 
finish button. Maybe it should be called

It could be good to choose oneself if extra 
blood glucose measurements should be

mething people have in common.

There could be a general pop-up which

Everyone should be able to no matter the

Appendix 15: 
Implementation meetings
Hedia
Vi har en række forskellige spørgsmål, som spæn­
der vidt, da Hedia er interessant for os at undersøge 
nærmere ift. flere forskellige elementer af vores 
opgave. Vi har løbende prøvet at kortlægge kon­
teksten omkring type 1 diabetes, og her er Hedia 
spændende for os, da appen for nogle kan være en 
central del af hverdagen med diabetes, og da Hedia 
er en del af den teknologiske udvikling inden for 
sygdommen.
Hedia og samarbejdspartnere
Hvordan samarbejder Hedia med Diabetesfor­
eningen?
Kontaktpersoner, og i forbindelse med deres tid­
ligere app, hvor hedia fik mere opmærksomhed, 
rykkede brugere til Hedia
Hvis nogle spørger dia har de henvist
de har stadig kulhydratstælling app - mange bruger 
stadig den sammen med Hedia, har været glade for 
billederne. Har vi ikke i hedia, kommer der nok 
heller ikke. Arbejder på standartmængder, lige nu 
gram - igangværende projekt
Indtil nu: Optimere backend, risk management 
(insulin beregner)
optimere udseende har været på pause
Louise sætter system i feedbacken fra brugere, har 
det liggende til når der er overskud i ressourcer
Er der nogen specifikke dele af appen som der sam­
arbejdes omkring?
ikke et dybdegående samarbejde med info frem og 
tilbage
mere at de anbefaler hedia
Samarbejder Hedia med nogen inden for det 
danske sundhedssystem? Hvem og hvorfor?
meget kontakt med novo nordisk, igang med udvik­
ling med novo, med smartpen der testes
sygeplejerske, intro certificeringskursus, hvor syge­
plejersker oplæres i at bruge app og sammen med 
patienter. Sikre brug og skabe opmærksomhed
gratis, det synes sygeplejerske er godt
Arbejder sammen med glucomen, contour nextone, 
ketomoto, (novo smartpen)
Hedia vil gerne være en del af det danske sund­
hedsvæsen
Hvordan bruges et eventuelt samarbejde til at 
udvikle Hedia appen?
Louise har taget op at samarbejde (co-creation), 
ikke i system
har bygget arkiv af forskellige former for fedback
har selv spurgt ind til brug og funktionaliteter hos 
sygeplejerske
back-end arbejde (medicinsk udstyr, højeste klas­
sificering), regulations skal prioriteres højest for at 
bi-beholde ce mærkning, har taget meget arbejde i 
det sidste års tid, meget maintenence, strukturering 
af back-end
mange gennem årene der ikke har levet op til krav 
og været opmærksomme på reguleringer
har ikke sat praksis i at hive folk ind - jeg opsamler 
det
udviklere kan kigge på feedback så snart der er et 
hul - små tweeks løbende
balance i at lytte og selv tage specialist hatten på
brugercentreret kan også blive en rode-butik
har hold af udviklere der arbejder efter roadmap
på vej hen imod et mere agilt setup hvor flere fag­
ligheder kan komme med input
Brugen af Hedia appen
Hvor mange brugere har Hedia cirka?
gør en del omkring markedsføring og skabe op­
mærksomhed plus arbejde med sygehus - sund­
hedsvæsnet kan ikke kun anbefale os, der er også 
andreer i 11 lande nu, for et par måneder siden blev 
det udvidethovedsageligt dk og england
4-5k brugere - håber på flere i de nye lande, men 
meget arbejde med positionering og go to market
power users - optimale antal insulin anbefalinger er 
4, sat ud fra undersøgelser der viser om det giver 
en gavnlig effekt
retrospective undersøgelse - fulgte brugere over 12 
uger - kan stabilisere ved brug af Hedia
fortsætter med kliniske studier for at bevise det 
kliniske Hedia
Hvilken aldersgruppe er jeres eksisterende bru­
gere?
blev reklameret som diabetes app
kan vælge type 2
er blevet mere skarpe på at få de rigtige brugere 
ind, insulinberegner er primær feature, ikke alle 
type 2 der har brug for insulinberegner - app er til 
folk som har insulinafhængig diabetes, primært 
type 1
aldersgruppe: +18, mest folk i lidt ældre (40+) i 
hvert fald dem jeg taler med, mange fra diabetes­
foreningen. Ikke bevidst valg, bør man kigge på, 
også ift at tiltrække yngre

Bruges Hedia appen som en aktiv del af behand­
lingsforløbet for personer med type 1 diabetes?
Hvad bruges den til i behandlingsforløbet? Fx 
som en logbog til at tracke data, som kan bruges 
i samtalen mellem behandler og patient?
Har I gjort jer nogen tanker omkring, om Hedia 
kunne bruges mere aktivt i behandlingen, end 
den gør nu?
arbejdede før hos center for kræft - spørgeskema 
man fik inden man kom, helhedsprofil. Aktive 
redskab som man skal snakke rundt om med be­
handler, nemt at gå tilbage i log - rapport, pdf fil, 
kunne være udgangspunktet for at samarbejde med 
behandlere
snakket med sygeplejersker, de bruger det for­
skelligt. Vigtigst er insulin dosis, beregner ud fra 
samlet daglig dosis
Kunne godt tænke sig (mål) at det bliver aktivt 
værktøj, som kan bruges til at monitorere patienter 
igennem - hvad skal der til? tid, arbejde, positione­
ring (kliniske studier)
bruger lige nu diasend - mange efterspørger om 
hedia kan integrere med diasend (ikke noget der 
arbejdes på), måske gennemsystemer se hedia data
Er der nogen begrænsninger i at integrere Hedia 
aktivt i behandlingen af type 1 diabetes? Fx relate­
ret til lovgivning eller etiske overvejelser.

Kliniske studier - lægemiddel sammen med virk­
somheder, men også med forskning. Primært hud­
sygdomme nu også diabetes.
Her er der behov for markedsanalyse frem for 
klinisk studie. Lidt en anden boldgade end det 
de laver. Studies&Me er stærke i det regulato­
riske space, med godkendelse - mest relevante i 
CE-mærkning.
Start-up miljøer mere relevant her.
Nogle der laver diæt, Hedia.
Indledende tests og overvejelser omkring feasibility
vigtigt at brugerne får noget tilbage.
Hvis vi får en masse brugere om bord og de siger ja 
til at vi kan bruge deres data, kan vi give data til fx 
novo og database i studies&me.
Tænke forretningside igennem før studies&me, 
måske der ikke er brug for kliniske studier.
Forretning - database - henrik vincent, james lind 
institute, database med diabetikere. Vi kan gemme 
data og spørge om de vil være med i forsøg - forret­
ningsmodel. Regulatoriske udfordringer, samtykke­
erklæringer.

men så har man stadig fællesskabet. Mange sund­
hedsapps bruges et par måneder og så er det regnet 
ud og man betaler ikke mere.

Formål:
-	
At bidrage til at studerende forstår hvil­
ke udfordringer personer med diabetes har og 
er med til at løse disse udfordringer (overordnet 
formål)
-	
At vi i Diabetesforeningen får viden og 
inspiration til de nyeste måder at få forståelse 
for vores medlemmers udfordringer og hvordan 
disse kan imødegås
-	
At der kommer konkrete, brugbare out­
puts til glæde og gavn for vores medlemmer, fx 
i form af nyheder, artikler i bladene, bladunder­
søgelser, rekruttering af medlemmer som en del 
af nogle projekter med efterfølgende kommuni­
kation, mere brugervenlig info på hjemmeside
-	
Øge vores samarbejde med eksterne, fx 
dem, der står for Forløbsplaner
-	
At de studerende får god vejledning og 
sparring hos os
Konkret info på siden, forslag:
1.	
Liste over forslag til projekter, herunder 
forslag fra tidl. studerende, arbejde videre på pro­
jekter, projekter formuleret af DBF
2.	
”Kom med forslag til projektidéer, så ser vi 
på det sammen”
3.	
Du kan forvente:
- en skrivebordsplads i F&A afdelingen min. 1-2 
dage om ugen, så du bliver en del af hverdagen
- statusmøde ½ time hver uge
- en fremlæggelse og diskussion af dit projekt for 
evt. andre studerende i DBF en gang om måneden
- kursus og anvendelse af spørgeskemaredskabet 
SurveyExact, hvis det er relevant
4.	
Emner for tidligere studieprojekter, alle 
med link til rapport, links til artikler, skemaer, 
vejledninger o.a. i DBF’s medier, hvor outputs fra 
projekterne indgår:
